â€˜â€˜YÄvakÄ«vaÃ±ca, bhikkhave, ime cha aparihÄniyÄ dhammÄ bhikkhÅ«su á¹­hassanti, imesu ca chasu aparihÄniyesu dhammesu bhikkhÅ« sandississanti, vuddhiyeva, bhikkhave, bhikkhÅ«naá¹ƒ pÄá¹­ikaá¹…khÄ, no parihÄnÄ«â€™â€™ti.

## SÄriputtasÄ«hanÄdo

### The Lion's Roar of SÄriputta.

145. Atha kho ÄyasmÄ sÄriputto yena bhagavÄ tenupasaá¹…kami; upasaá¹…kamitvÄ bhagavantaá¹ƒ abhivÄdetvÄ ekamantaá¹ƒ nisÄ«di. Ekamantaá¹ƒ nisinno kho ÄyasmÄ sÄriputto bhagavantaá¹ƒ etadavoca â€“ â€˜â€˜evaá¹ƒ pasanno ahaá¹ƒ, bhante, bhagavati; na cÄhu na ca bhavissati na cetarahi vijjati aÃ±Ã±o samaá¹‡o vÄ brÄhmaá¹‡o vÄ bhagavatÄ bhiyyobhiÃ±Ã±ataro yadidaá¹ƒ sambodhiyaâ€™â€™nti. â€˜â€˜Uá¸·ÄrÄ kho te ayaá¹ƒ, sÄriputta, ÄsabhÄ« vÄcÄ [ÄsabhivÄcÄ (syÄ.)] bhÄsitÄ, ekaá¹ƒso gahito, sÄ«hanÄdo nadito â€“ â€˜evaá¹ƒpasanno ahaá¹ƒ, bhante, bhagavati; na cÄhu na ca bhavissati na cetarahi vijjati aÃ±Ã±o samaá¹‡o vÄ brÄhmaá¹‡o vÄ bhagavatÄ bhiyyobhiÃ±Ã±ataro yadidaá¹ƒ sambodhiyaâ€™nti.

145.Then Venerable SÄriputta approached the Blessed One. Having approached, he paid homage to the Blessed One and sat down to one side. Sitting to one side, Venerable SÄriputta said this to the Blessed One: "I have such faith in the Blessed One, venerable sir, that I believe there never has been, never will be, and there is not now, another ascetic or brahmin more greatly enlightened than the Blessed One with respect to supreme enlightenment." "Grand and bold, SÄriputta, is this speech of yours, a categorical assertion, a veritable lion's roar: 'I have such faith in the Blessed One, venerable sir, that I believe there never has been, never will be, and there is not now, another ascetic or brahmin more greatly enlightened than the Blessed One with respect to supreme enlightenment.'"

â€˜â€˜Kiá¹ƒ te [kiá¹ƒ nu (syÄ. pÄ«. ka.)], sÄriputta, ye te ahesuá¹ƒ atÄ«tamaddhÄnaá¹ƒ arahanto sammÄsambuddhÄ, sabbe te bhagavanto cetasÄ ceto paricca viditÄ â€“ â€˜evaá¹ƒsÄ«lÄ te bhagavanto ahesuá¹ƒ itipi, evaá¹ƒdhammÄ evaá¹ƒpaÃ±Ã±Ä evaá¹ƒvihÄrÄ« evaá¹ƒvimuttÄ te bhagavanto ahesuá¹ƒ itipÄ«â€™â€™â€™ti? â€˜â€˜No hetaá¹ƒ, bhanteâ€™â€™.

What do you think, SÄriputta, were all those Blessed Ones, Arahants, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones of the past known to you by encompassing their minds with your mindâ€”'Such was their virtue, such their Dhamma, such their wisdom, such their abiding, such their liberation'?

â€˜â€˜Kiá¹ƒ pana te [kiá¹ƒ pana (syÄ. pÄ«. ka.)], sÄriputta, ye te bhavissanti anÄgatamaddhÄnaá¹ƒ arahanto sammÄsambuddhÄ, sabbe te bhagavanto cetasÄ ceto paricca viditÄ â€“ â€˜evaá¹ƒsÄ«lÄ te bhagavanto bhavissanti itipi, evaá¹ƒdhammÄ evaá¹ƒpaÃ±Ã±Ä evaá¹ƒvihÄrÄ« evaá¹ƒvimuttÄ te bhagavanto bhavissanti itipÄ«â€™â€™â€™ti? â€˜â€˜No hetaá¹ƒ, bhanteâ€™â€™.

â€˜â€˜Kiá¹ƒ pana te, sÄriputta, ahaá¹ƒ etarahi arahaá¹ƒ sammÄsambuddho cetasÄ ceto paricca vidito â€“ â€˜â€˜evaá¹ƒsÄ«lo bhagavÄ itipi, evaá¹ƒdhammo evaá¹ƒpaÃ±Ã±o evaá¹ƒvihÄrÄ« evaá¹ƒvimutto bhagavÄ itipÄ«â€™â€™â€™ti? â€˜â€˜No hetaá¹ƒ, bhanteâ€™â€™.

â€˜â€˜Ettha ca hi te, sÄriputta, atÄ«tÄnÄgatapaccuppannesu arahantesu sammÄsambuddhesu cetopariyaÃ±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ [cetopariÃ±Ã±ÄyaÃ±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ (syÄ.), cetasÄ cetopariyÄyaÃ±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ (ka.)] natthi. Atha kiÃ±carahi te ayaá¹ƒ, sÄriputta, uá¸·ÄrÄ ÄsabhÄ« vÄcÄ bhÄsitÄ, ekaá¹ƒso gahito, sÄ«hanÄdo nadito â€“ â€˜evaá¹ƒpasanno ahaá¹ƒ, bhante, bhagavati; na cÄhu na ca bhavissati na cetarahi vijjati aÃ±Ã±o samaá¹‡o vÄ brÄhmaá¹‡o vÄ bhagavatÄ bhiyyobhiÃ±Ã±ataro yadidaá¹ƒ sambodhiyaâ€™â€™â€™nti?

Here, SÄriputta, you have no knowledge of the minds of others regarding the Arahants, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones of the past, future, and present. 146. â€˜â€˜Na kho me, bhante, atÄ«tÄnÄgatapaccuppannesu arahantesu sammÄsambuddhesu cetopariyaÃ±Äá¹‡aá¹ƒ atthi, api ca me dhammanvayo vidito. SeyyathÄpi, bhante, raÃ±Ã±o paccantimaá¹ƒ nagaraá¹ƒ daá¸·huddhÄpaá¹ƒ daá¸·hapÄkÄratoraá¹‡aá¹ƒ ekadvÄraá¹ƒ, tatrassa dovÄriko paá¹‡á¸ito viyatto medhÄvÄ« aÃ±Ã±ÄtÄnaá¹ƒ nivÄretÄ Ã±ÄtÄnaá¹ƒ pavesetÄ. BhagavÄpi, bhante, etarahi arahaá¹ƒ sammÄsambuddho paÃ±ca nÄ«varaá¹‡e pahÄya cetaso upakkilese paÃ±Ã±Äya dubbalÄ«karaá¹‡e catÅ«su satipaá¹­á¹­hÄnesu supatiá¹­á¹­hitacitto satta bojjhaá¹…ge yathÄbhÅ«taá¹ƒ bhÄvetvÄ anuttaraá¹ƒ sammÄsambodhiá¹ƒ abhisambuddhoâ€™â€™â€™ti.

146.Venerable sir, I do not possess knowledge of the minds of others regarding the Arahants, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones of the past, future, and present, but I have understood the lineage of the Dhamma. Just as, venerable sir, a king's frontier city might have strong foundations, strong walls and gate-towers, with a single gate, and there would be a gatekeeper who is wise, competent, and intelligent, one who keeps out strangers and admits acquaintances. As he patrols around the city's perimeter, he would not see any crack or gap in the wall, not even one big enough for a cat to slip through. He would think: 'Whatever gross creatures enter or leave this city, all do so only by this gate.' In the same way, venerable sir, I have understood the lineage of the Dhamma: 'All those Blessed Ones, Arahants, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones who were in the past abandoned the five hindrancesâ€”defilements of the mind that weaken wisdomâ€”firmly established their minds in the four foundations of mindfulness, and developed the seven factors of enlightenment as they really are; they all awakened to unsurpassed perfect enlightenment. All those Blessed Ones, Arahants, Perfectly Self-Enlightened Ones who will be in the future will abandon the five hindrancesâ€”defilements of the mind that weaken wisdomâ€”firmly establish their minds in the four foundations of mindfulness, and develop the seven factors of enlightenment as they really are; they too will awaken to unsurpassed perfect enlightenment. The Blessed One, venerable sir, who is now the Arahant, the Perfectly Self-Enlightened One, has abandoned the five hindrancesâ€”defilements of the mind that weaken wisdomâ€”firmly established his mind in the four foundations of mindfulness, and developed the seven factors of enlightenment as they really are; he has awakened to unsurpassed perfect enlightenment.'"

147. Tatrapi sudaá¹ƒ bhagavÄ nÄá¸·andÄyaá¹ƒ viharanto pÄvÄrikambavane etadeva bahulaá¹ƒ bhikkhÅ«naá¹ƒ dhammiá¹ƒ kathaá¹ƒ karoti â€“ â€˜â€˜iti sÄ«laá¹ƒ, iti samÄdhi, iti paÃ±Ã±Ä. SÄ«laparibhÄvito samÄdhi mahapphalo hoti mahÄnisaá¹ƒso. SamÄdhiparibhÄvitÄ paÃ±Ã±Ä mahapphalÄ hoti mahÄnisaá¹ƒsÄ. PaÃ±Ã±ÄparibhÄvitaá¹ƒ cittaá¹ƒ sammadeva Äsavehi vimuccati, seyyathidaá¹ƒ â€“ kÄmÄsavÄ, bhavÄsavÄ, avijjÄsavÄâ€™â€™ti.

147.There too, it is said, while the Blessed One was dwelling at NÄá¸·andÄ in PÄvÄrika's mango grove, he frequently gave this Dhamma talk to the bhikkhus: "Such is virtue, such is concentration, such is wisdom. Concentration, when cultivated by virtue, is of great fruit and great benefit. Wisdom, when cultivated by concentration, is of great fruit and great benefit. The mind, when cultivated by wisdom, is utterly freed from the taints, namely, the taint of sensual desire, the taint of existence, and the taint of ignorance."

148.Then the Blessed One, having stayed at NÄá¸·andÄ as long as he pleased, addressed Venerable Ä€nanda: â€œCome, Ä€nanda, let us approach PÄá¹­aligÄma.â€ â€œYes, Venerable Sir,â€ replied Venerable Ä€nanda to the Blessed One. 149. Atha kho bhagavÄ pÄá¹­aligÄmike upÄsake Ämantesi â€“ â€˜â€˜paÃ±cime, gahapatayo, ÄdÄ«navÄ dussÄ«lassa sÄ«lavipattiyÄ. Katame paÃ±ca? Idha, gahapatayo, dussÄ«lo sÄ«lavipanno pamÄdÄdhikaraá¹‡aá¹ƒ mahatiá¹ƒ bhogajÄniá¹ƒ nigacchati. Ayaá¹ƒ paá¹­hamo ÄdÄ«navo dussÄ«lassa sÄ«lavipattiyÄ.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, gahapatayo, dussÄ«lassa sÄ«lavipannassa pÄpako kittisaddo abbhuggacchati. Ayaá¹ƒ dutiyo ÄdÄ«navo dussÄ«lassa sÄ«lavipattiyÄ.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, gahapatayo, dussÄ«lo sÄ«lavipanno sammÅ«á¸·ho kÄlaá¹…karoti. Ayaá¹ƒ catuttho ÄdÄ«navo dussÄ«lassa sÄ«lavipattiyÄ.

## SÄ«lavantaÄnisaá¹ƒsa

### The Benefits of Virtue

150. â€˜â€˜PaÃ±cime, gahapatayo, Änisaá¹ƒsÄ sÄ«lavato sÄ«lasampadÄya. Katame paÃ±ca? Idha, gahapatayo, sÄ«lavÄ sÄ«lasampanno appamÄdÄdhikaraá¹‡aá¹ƒ mahantaá¹ƒ bhogakkhandhaá¹ƒ adhigacchati. Ayaá¹ƒ paá¹­hamo Änisaá¹ƒso sÄ«lavato sÄ«lasampadÄya.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, gahapatayo, sÄ«lavÄ sÄ«lasampanno asammÅ«á¸·ho kÄlaá¹…karoti. Ayaá¹ƒ catuttho Änisaá¹ƒso sÄ«lavato sÄ«lasampadÄya.

Atha kho bhagavÄ pÄá¹­aligÄmike upÄsake bahudeva rattiá¹ƒ dhammiyÄ kathÄya sandassetvÄ samÄdapetvÄ samuttejetvÄ sampahaá¹ƒsetvÄ uyyojesi â€“ â€˜â€˜abhikkantÄ kho, gahapatayo, ratti, yassadÄni tumhe kÄlaá¹ƒ maÃ±Ã±athÄâ€™â€™ti. â€˜â€˜Evaá¹ƒ, bhanteâ€™â€™ti kho pÄá¹­aligÄmikÄ upÄsakÄ bhagavato paá¹­issutvÄ uá¹­á¹­hÄyÄsanÄ bhagavantaá¹ƒ abhivÄdetvÄ padakkhiá¹‡aá¹ƒ katvÄ pakkamiá¹ƒsu. ## PÄá¹­aliputtanagaramÄpanaá¹ƒ

### The Building of the City of PÄá¹­aliputta

152.Now at that time, Sunidha and VassakÄra, the chief ministers of Magadha, were building a city at PÄá¹­aligÄma to keep the Vajjis at bay. Atha kho bhagavÄ pubbaá¹‡hasamayaá¹ƒ nivÄsetvÄ pattacÄ«varamÄdÄya saddhiá¹ƒ bhikkhusaá¹…ghena yena sunidhavassakÄrÄnaá¹ƒ magadhamahÄmattÄnaá¹ƒ Ävasatho tenupasaá¹…kami; upasaá¹…kamitvÄ paÃ±Ã±atte Äsane nisÄ«di. 154.Now at that time, Sunidha and VassakÄra, the chief ministers of Magadha, were following closely behind the Blessed One, thinking: "The gate by which the ascetic Gotama leaves today will be called the Gotama Gate. "Those who cross the ocean and the lake, having made a bridge, abandoning the marshes;

## DhammÄdÄsadhammapariyÄyÄ

### The Mirror of the Dhamma: A Discourse on the Dhamma

158. â€˜â€˜Anacchariyaá¹ƒ kho panetaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yaá¹ƒ manussabhÅ«to kÄlaá¹…kareyya. Tasmiá¹ƒyeva [tasmiá¹ƒ tasmiá¹ƒ ce (sÄ«. pÄ«.), tasmiá¹ƒ tasmiá¹ƒ kho (syÄ.)] kÄlaá¹…kate tathÄgataá¹ƒ upasaá¹…kamitvÄ etamatthaá¹ƒ pucchissatha, vihesÄ hesÄ, Änanda, tathÄgatassa. 158."It is no wonder, Ä€nanda, that a human being should die. But if, when one has died, you were to come to the TathÄgata and ask about this matter, that would be tiresome for the TathÄgata. â€˜â€˜Ayaá¹ƒ kho so, Änanda, dhammÄdÄso dhammapariyÄyo, yena samannÄgato ariyasÄvako Äkaá¹…khamÄno attanÄva attÄnaá¹ƒ byÄkareyya â€“ â€˜khÄ«á¹‡anirayomhi khÄ«á¹‡atiracchÄnayoni khÄ«á¹‡apettivisayo khÄ«á¹‡ÄpÄyaduggativinipÄto, sotÄpannohamasmi avinipÄtadhammo niyato sambodhiparÄyaá¹‡oâ€™â€™â€™ti.

â€˜â€˜Iti sÄ«laá¹ƒ iti samÄdhi iti paÃ±Ã±Ä. SÄ«laparibhÄvito samÄdhi mahapphalo hoti mahÄnisaá¹ƒso. SamÄdhiparibhÄvitÄ paÃ±Ã±Ä mahapphalÄ hoti mahÄnisaá¹ƒsÄ. PaÃ±Ã±ÄparibhÄvitaá¹ƒ cittaá¹ƒ sammadeva Äsavehi vimuccati, seyyathidaá¹ƒ â€“ kÄmÄsavÄ, bhavÄsavÄ, avijjÄsavÄâ€™â€™ti.

"Thus is virtue, thus is concentration, thus is wisdom. Concentration, developed with virtue, is of great fruit and great benefit. "Mindful, bhikkhus, should a bhikkhu dwell, clearly comprehending; this is our instruction to you. And how, bhikkhus, is a bhikkhu mindful? Here, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu dwells contemplating the body in the body, ardent, clearly comprehending, ever mindful, having removed covetousness and displeasure in regard to the world. â€˜â€˜KathaÃ±ca, bhikkhave, bhikkhu sampajÄno hoti? "And how, bhikkhus, is a bhikkhu clearly comprehending? 165.But what, Ä€nanda, does the Saá¹…gha of monks expect from me? The Dhamma has been taught by me, Ä€nanda, without making any distinction between inner and outer. There is no closed fist of the teacher, Ä€nanda, in the teachings of the TathÄgata. So why should the TathÄgata make any declaration concerning the Saá¹…gha of monks? Now I, Ä€nanda, am old, aged, burdened with years, advanced in life, and have reached the end of my days. I am eighty years old. Just as, Ä€nanda, an old cart is made to move by being held together with straps, so too, Ä€nanda, the body of the TathÄgata is kept going, I think, by being strapped together. Here, Ä€nanda, a monk dwells contemplating the body in the body, ardent, clearly comprehending, mindful, having removed covetousness and displeasure in regard to the world. He dwells contemplating feelings in feelingsâ€¦ mind in mindâ€¦ phenomena in phenomena, ardent, clearly comprehending, mindful, having removed covetousness and displeasure in regard to the world. It is in this way, Ä€nanda, that a monk dwells with himself as his island, himself as his refuge, with no other refuge; with the Dhamma as his island, the Dhamma as his refuge, with no other refuge. Those monks, Ä€nanda, who now or after I am gone dwell with themselves as their island, themselves as their refuge, with no other refuge; with the Dhamma as their island, the Dhamma as their refuge, with no other refugeâ€”these monks, Ä€nanda, shall be the foremost among those who are desirous of training."

Ananda, whoever has developed, cultivated, made a vehicle, made a basis, established, consolidated, and properly undertaken the four bases of spiritual power, if they so wish, they could live for an aeon or the remainder of an aeon. If he so wished, the TathÄgata could live for an aeon or the remainder of an aeon.â€ Yet again, though the Blessed One gave such an obvious hint and clear signal, Venerable Ananda failed to grasp it. He rose from his seat, paid homage to the Blessed One, circumambulated him, and sat down at the foot of a tree not far away.

## MahÄbhÅ«micÄlahetu

### The Cause of the Great Earthquake

170. Atha kho Äyasmato Änandassa etadahosi â€“ â€˜â€˜acchariyaá¹ƒ vata bho, abbhutaá¹ƒ vata bho, mahÄ vatÄyaá¹ƒ bhÅ«micÄlo; sumahÄ vatÄyaá¹ƒ bhÅ«micÄlo bhiá¹ƒsanako salomahaá¹ƒso; devadundubhiyo ca phaliá¹ƒsu. Ko nu kho hetu ko paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄyÄâ€™â€™ti?

Then Venerable Ä€nanda approached the Blessed One, and after approaching and paying homage to him, sat down to one side. How very great indeed is this earthquake, venerable sir, terrifying and hair-raising! And the divine drums burst forth. 171. â€˜â€˜Aá¹­á¹­ha kho ime, Änanda, hetÅ«, aá¹­á¹­ha paccayÄ mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya. Katame aá¹­á¹­ha? Ayaá¹ƒ, Änanda, mahÄpathavÄ« udake patiá¹­á¹­hitÄ, udakaá¹ƒ vÄte patiá¹­á¹­hitaá¹ƒ, vÄto ÄkÄsaá¹­á¹­ho. Hoti kho so, Änanda, samayo, yaá¹ƒ mahÄvÄtÄ vÄyanti. MahÄvÄtÄ vÄyantÄ udakaá¹ƒ kampenti. 171."There are, Ananda, these eight causes, these eight conditions for the appearance of a great earthquake. What are the eight? This great earth, Ananda, is established on water; the water is established on wind; the wind is established on space. There comes a time, Ananda, when great winds blow. As great winds blow, they agitate the water. The agitated water agitates the earth. This is the first cause, the first condition for the appearance of a great earthquake.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, samaá¹‡o vÄ hoti brÄhmaá¹‡o vÄ iddhimÄ cetovasippatto, devo vÄ mahiddhiko mahÄnubhÄvo, tassa parittÄ pathavÄ«saÃ±Ã±Ä bhÄvitÄ hoti, appamÄá¹‡Ä ÄposaÃ±Ã±Ä. "Furthermore, Ananda, a monk or brahmin who has psychic power and has attained mastery of mind, or a powerful and mighty deity, has developed a limited earth perception and a limitless water perception. They can shake, quake, and violently convulse this earth. This is the second cause, the second condition for the appearance of a great earthquake."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ bodhisatto tusitakÄyÄ cavitvÄ sato sampajÄno mÄtukucchiá¹ƒ okkamati, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. Ayaá¹ƒ tatiyo hetu tatiyo paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya.

"Furthermore, Ananda, when the Bodhisatta, mindful and clearly comprehending, passes away from the Tusita realm and descends into his mother's womb, then this earth shakes, trembles, and quakes violently. This is the third cause, the third condition for the appearance of a great earthquake."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ bodhisatto sato sampajÄno mÄtukucchismÄ nikkhamati, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. Ayaá¹ƒ catuttho hetu catuttho paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya.

"Furthermore, Ananda, when the Bodhisatta, mindful and clearly comprehending, emerges from his mother's womb, then this earth shakes, quakes, and trembles. This is the fourth cause, the fourth condition for the appearance of a great earthquake."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ tathÄgato anuttaraá¹ƒ sammÄsambodhiá¹ƒ abhisambujjhati, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. Ayaá¹ƒ paÃ±camo hetu paÃ±camo paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya.

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ tathÄgato anuttaraá¹ƒ dhammacakkaá¹ƒ pavatteti, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. Ayaá¹ƒ chaá¹­á¹­ho hetu chaá¹­á¹­ho paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya.

"Furthermore, Ananda, when the Tathagata sets in motion the unsurpassed Wheel of Dhamma, then this earth shakes, quakes, and trembles. This is the sixth cause, the sixth condition for the appearance of a great earthquake."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ tathÄgato sato sampajÄno Äyusaá¹…khÄraá¹ƒ ossajjati, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. Ayaá¹ƒ sattamo hetu sattamo paccayo mahato bhÅ«micÄlassa pÄtubhÄvÄya.

"Furthermore, Ananda, when the Tathagata, mindful and clearly comprehending, relinquishes the life-formation, then this earth shakes, trembles, and violently quakes. This is the seventh cause, the seventh condition for the appearance of a great earthquake."

â€˜â€˜Puna caparaá¹ƒ, Änanda, yadÄ tathÄgato anupÄdisesÄya nibbÄnadhÄtuyÄ parinibbÄyati, tadÄyaá¹ƒ pathavÄ« kampati saá¹…kampati sampakampati sampavedhati. "Furthermore, Ananda, when the Tathagata attains final NibbÄna with no residue remaining, then this earth shakes, quakes, and trembles violently. This is the eighth cause, the eighth condition for the appearance of a great earthquake. These, Ananda, are the eight causes, the eight conditions for the appearance of a great earthquake."

172."There are these eight assemblies, Ä€nanda. Which eight? 174.â€œThere are, Ä€nanda, these eight liberations. What are the eight? One possessing form sees forms; this is the first liberation. 183."Ananda, have I not already told you that separation, parting, and otherness are the nature of all things dear and beloved? â€œHere, bhikkhus, suppose a bhikkhu were to say: â€˜In such and such a monastery, many elder bhikkhus dwell who are learned, versed in the traditions, upholders of the Dhamma, upholders of the Vinaya, upholders of the MÄtikÄ. â€˜â€˜Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu evaá¹ƒ vadeyya â€“ â€˜amukasmiá¹ƒ nÄma ÄvÄse eko thero bhikkhu viharati bahussuto ÄgatÄgamo dhammadharo vinayadharo mÄtikÄdharo. â€œHere, bhikkhus, a bhikkhu might speak thus: â€˜In such and such a dwelling place there dwells an elder bhikkhu who is learned, who has mastered the traditions, a Dhamma-bearer, a Vinaya-bearer, a MÄtikÄ-bearer. 193."What do you think, Pukkusa, which is more difficult and harder to achieveâ€”someone who is conscious and awake not seeing or hearing five hundred carts passing by one after another, or someone who is conscious and awake not seeing or hearing when it is raining, when thunder is rumbling, when lightning is darting, and when thunderbolts are cracking?" 197.Then the Blessed One addressed Venerable Ä€nanda: "Ä€nanda, it is possible that someone might arouse remorse in Cunda the smith's son, saying: â€˜It is your loss, friend Cunda, it is your misfortune that the TathÄgata, having eaten his last alms-meal from you, attained final NibbÄna.â€™ Ä€nanda, the remorse of Cunda the smith's son should be dispelled thus: â€˜It is your gain, friend Cunda, it is your good fortune that the TathÄgata, having eaten his last alms-meal from you, attained final NibbÄna. 205."But how, venerable sir, should the TathÄgata's body be treated?" "Just as, Ä€nanda, the body of a universal monarch is treated, so should the TathÄgata's body be treated." "But how, venerable sir, is the body of a universal monarch treated?" "Ä€nanda, the body of a universal monarch is wrapped in new cloth; having wrapped it in new cloth, they wrap it with carded cotton; having wrapped it with carded cotton, they wrap it again with new cloth. In this way, the body of a universal monarch is wrapped in five hundred layers, then placed in a golden oil-trough and covered with another golden trough. A pyre of all kinds of fragrant woods is made, and the body of the universal monarch is cremated. At the four great crossroads, a stupa is built for the universal monarch. Thus, Ä€nanda, the body of a universal monarch is treated. Just as the body of a universal monarch is treated, so should the TathÄgata's body be treated. At the four great crossroads, a stupa should be built for the TathÄgata. There, whoever offers garlands, incense, or powder, or makes salutations, or inspires confidence in their mind, that will be for their long-term welfare and happiness."

Formerly, Ä€nanda, there was a king named MahÄsudassana, a wheel-turning monarch, a righteous king of Dhamma, conqueror of the four quarters, who had established the country in security, endowed with the seven treasures. â€˜â€˜Gaccha tvaá¹ƒ, Änanda, kusinÄraá¹ƒ pavisitvÄ kosinÄrakÄnaá¹ƒ mallÄnaá¹ƒ Ärocehi â€“ â€˜ajja kho, vÄseá¹­á¹­hÄ, rattiyÄ pacchime yÄme tathÄgatassa parinibbÄnaá¹ƒ bhavissati. 211.Now at that time the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ had gathered in the assembly hall for some business. Then Venerable Ä€nanda approached the assembly hall of the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ. Thus, by this means, Venerable Ä€nanda had all the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ pay homage to the Blessed One during the first watch of the night.

214.â€œSubhadda, in whatever teaching and discipline the Noble Eightfold Path is not found, neither a first ascetic is found, nor a second ascetic is found, nor a third ascetic is found, nor a fourth ascetic is found. 215.When this was said, the wanderer Subhadda said to the Blessed One: â€œExcellent, venerable sir! Excellent, venerable sir! 217.Then the Blessed One addressed the monks: â€œMonks, should even a single monk have any doubt or uncertainty about the Buddha, the Dhamma, the Saá¹…gha, the path, or the practice, ask now, monks. ## ParinibbutakathÄ

### The Account of the Final NibbÄna

219. Atha kho bhagavÄ paá¹­hamaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, paá¹­hamajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ dutiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, dutiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ tatiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, tatiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ catutthaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji. CatutthajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ ÄkiÃ±caÃ±Ã±Äyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, ÄkiÃ±caÃ±Ã±ÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ nevasaÃ±Ã±ÄnÄsaÃ±Ã±Äyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, nevasaÃ±Ã±ÄnÄsaÃ±Ã±ÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ saÃ±Ã±Ävedayitanirodhaá¹ƒ samÄpajji.

219.Then the Blessed One entered the first jhana. Emerging from the first jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, he entered the base of infinite space. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite space, he entered the base of infinite consciousness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite consciousness, he entered the base of nothingness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of nothingness, he entered the base of neither perception nor non-perception. Emerging from the attainment of the base of neither perception nor non-perception, he entered the cessation of perception and feeling.

Atha kho ÄyasmÄ Änando Äyasmantaá¹ƒ anuruddhaá¹ƒ etadavoca â€“ â€˜â€˜parinibbuto, bhante anuruddha, bhagavÄâ€™â€™ti. â€˜â€˜NÄvuso Änanda, bhagavÄ parinibbuto, saÃ±Ã±Ävedayitanirodhaá¹ƒ samÄpannoâ€™â€™ti.

Then the Venerable Ä€nanda said to the Venerable Anuruddha: "Venerable Anuruddha, has the Blessed One passed away into final NibbÄna?" "No, friend Ä€nanda, the Blessed One has not passed away into final NibbÄna; he has entered the cessation of perception and feeling."

Atha kho bhagavÄ saÃ±Ã±ÄvedayitanirodhasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ nevasaÃ±Ã±ÄnÄsaÃ±Ã±Äyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, nevasaÃ±Ã±ÄnÄsaÃ±Ã±ÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ ÄkiÃ±caÃ±Ã±Äyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, ÄkiÃ±caÃ±Ã±ÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, viÃ±Ã±Äá¹‡aÃ±cÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, ÄkÄsÄnaÃ±cÄyatanasamÄpattiyÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ catutthaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, catutthajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ tatiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, tatiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ dutiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, dutiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ paá¹­hamaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, paá¹­hamajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ dutiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, dutiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ tatiyaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, tatiyajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ catutthaá¹ƒ jhÄnaá¹ƒ samÄpajji, catutthajjhÄnÄ vuá¹­á¹­hahitvÄ samanantarÄ bhagavÄ parinibbÄyi.

Then the Blessed One, emerging from the attainment of the cessation of perception and feeling, entered the base of neither perception nor non-perception. Emerging from the attainment of the base of neither perception nor non-perception, he entered the base of nothingness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of nothingness, he entered the base of infinite consciousness. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite consciousness, he entered the base of infinite space. Emerging from the attainment of the base of infinite space, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the first jhana. Emerging from the first jhana, he entered the second jhana. Emerging from the second jhana, he entered the third jhana. Emerging from the third jhana, he entered the fourth jhana. Emerging from the fourth jhana, the Blessed One immediately passed away into final NibbÄna.

220. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbÄnÄ mahÄbhÅ«micÄlo ahosi bhiá¹ƒsanako salomahaá¹ƒso. Devadundubhiyo ca phaliá¹ƒsu. Parinibbute bhagavati saha parinibbÄnÄ brahmÄsahampati imaá¹ƒ gÄthaá¹ƒ abhÄsi â€“

220.When the Blessed One passed away into final NibbÄna, simultaneously with his passing away into final NibbÄna there was a great earthquake, dreadful and hair-raising, and the drums of the gods resounded. â€˜â€˜Sabbeva nikkhipissanti, bhÅ«tÄ loke samussayaá¹ƒ;Yattha etÄdiso satthÄ, loke appaá¹­ipuggalo;TathÄgato balappatto, sambuddho parinibbutoâ€™â€™ti.

"All beings in the world will lay down this accumulation. Where even such a Teacher, without a peer in the world, the TathÄgata, possessed of strength, the Perfectly Enlightened One, has passed away into final NibbÄna!"

â€˜â€˜AniccÄ vata saá¹…khÄrÄ, uppÄdavayadhammino;UppajjitvÄ nirujjhanti, tesaá¹ƒ vÅ«pasamo sukhoâ€™â€™ti.

"Impermanent, indeed, are conditioned things, subject to arising and passing away. Having arisen, they cease; their stilling is bliss."

â€˜â€˜AsallÄ«nena cittena, vedanaá¹ƒ ajjhavÄsayi;Pajjotasseva nibbÄnaá¹ƒ, vimokkho cetaso ahÅ«â€™â€™ti.

224.When the Blessed One had passed away into final NibbÄna, some monks there who were not free from passion stretched out their arms and wept, collapsed, rolled back and forth, lamenting, "Too soon the Blessed One has passed away into final NibbÄna! 225. Atha kho ÄyasmÄ anuruddho bhikkhÅ« Ämantesi â€“ â€˜â€˜alaá¹ƒ, Ävuso, mÄ socittha mÄ paridevittha. 225.Then Venerable Anuruddha addressed the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. Where could this be found, friends, that what is born, become, conditioned, subject to decay, should not decay? Such a thing is not possible. The deities, friends, are murmuring." "But what kind of deities, Venerable Anuruddha, are you attending to in your mind?"

â€˜â€˜SantÄvuso Änanda, devatÄ ÄkÄse pathavÄ«saÃ±Ã±iniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bÄhÄ paggayha kandanti, chinnapÄtaá¹ƒ papatanti, Ävaá¹­á¹­anti, vivaá¹­á¹­anti â€“ â€˜atikhippaá¹ƒ bhagavÄ parinibbuto, atikhippaá¹ƒ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaá¹ƒ cakkhuá¹ƒ loke antarahitoâ€™ti. SantÄvuso Änanda, devatÄ pathaviyÄ pathavÄ«saÃ±Ã±iniyo kese pakiriya kandanti, bÄhÄ paggayha kandanti, chinnapÄtaá¹ƒ papatanti, Ävaá¹­á¹­anti, vivaá¹­á¹­anti â€“ â€˜atikhippaá¹ƒ bhagavÄ parinibbuto, atikhippaá¹ƒ sugato parinibbuto, atikhippaá¹ƒ cakkhuá¹ƒ loke antarahitoâ€™ti. "Friend Ananda, there are deities in the sky who perceive the earth, tearing their hair, wailing, raising their arms, falling down as if cut down, rolling and tossing about, crying: 'Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Eye of the World vanished!' Friend Ananda, there are deities on the earth who perceive the earth, tearing their hair, wailing, raising their arms, falling down as if cut down, rolling and tossing about, crying: 'Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Eye of the World vanished!' But those deities who are free from passion remain mindful and composed, reflecting: 'Impermanent are conditioned things; how could it be otherwise?' Then the Venerable Anuruddha and the Venerable Ananda spent the rest of the night in religious discussion."

226. Atha kho ÄyasmÄ anuruddho Äyasmantaá¹ƒ Änandaá¹ƒ Ämantesi â€“ â€˜â€˜gacchÄvuso Änanda, kusinÄraá¹ƒ pavisitvÄ kosinÄrakÄnaá¹ƒ mallÄnaá¹ƒ Ärocehi â€“ â€˜parinibbuto, vÄseá¹­á¹­hÄ, bhagavÄ, yassadÄni kÄlaá¹ƒ maÃ±Ã±athÄâ€™â€™â€™ti. â€˜â€˜Evaá¹ƒ, bhanteâ€™â€™ti kho ÄyasmÄ Änando Äyasmato anuruddhassa paá¹­issutvÄ pubbaá¹‡hasamayaá¹ƒ nivÄsetvÄ pattacÄ«varamÄdÄya attadutiyo kusinÄraá¹ƒ pÄvisi. 226.Then the Venerable Anuruddha addressed the Venerable Ä€nanda: "Go, friend Ä€nanda, enter KusinÄrÄ and announce to the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ: 'The Blessed One, VÄseá¹­á¹­has, has passed away into final NibbÄna. Then the Venerable Ä€nanda approached the assembly hall of the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ and announced to them: "The Blessed One, VÄseá¹­á¹­has, has passed away into final NibbÄna. Now is the time as you think fit." Some tore their hair and wept, some stretched out their arms and wailed, some fell prostrate as if cut down, rolling back and forth, crying: "Too soon has the Blessed One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Sublime One passed away into final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Eye in the World vanished!"

## MahÄkassapattheravatthu

### The Story of Venerable MahÄkassapa

231. Tena kho pana samayena ÄyasmÄ mahÄkassapo pÄvÄya kusinÄraá¹ƒ addhÄnamaggappaá¹­ippanno hoti mahatÄ bhikkhusaá¹…ghena saddhiá¹ƒ paÃ±camattehi bhikkhusatehi. 231.At that time, Venerable MahÄkassapa was traveling on the road from PÄvÄ to KusinÄrÄ with a large company of about five hundred monks. Then, Venerable MahÄkassapa left the road and sat down at the foot of a certain tree. At that time, a certain Ä€jÄ«vaka was traveling on the road from KusinÄrÄ to PÄvÄ, carrying a mandÄrava flower. There, those monks who were not free from passion wept, raising their arms, collapsing as if cut down, rolling back and forth, crying, "Too soon has the Blessed One attained final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Fortunate One attained final NibbÄna! Too soon has the Eye in the world disappeared!" But those monks who were free from passion, mindful and fully aware, endured, reflecting: "All conditioned things are impermanent; how could it be otherwise?"

232.Now at that time, Subhadda, an old renunciant, was sitting in that assembly. Then Subhadda, the old renunciant, said this to the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. We are well rid of that great ascetic. We were harassed by him: 'This is permissible for you, this is not permissible for you.' But now we will do what we want, and we will not do what we do not want."Then Venerable MahÄkassapa addressed the monks: "Enough, friends, do not grieve, do not lament. Has not the Blessed One declared this beforehand: 'Separation, disunion, and otherness are inevitable with all that is dear and beloved'? How could it be otherwise, friends? It is impossible that this should be: 'May the body of the Tathagata not disintegrate,' when it is something born, come into being, compounded, and subject to decay."

233. Tena kho pana samayena cattÄro mallapÄmokkhÄ sÄ«saá¹ƒnhÄtÄ ahatÄni vatthÄni nivatthÄ â€“ â€˜â€˜mayaá¹ƒ bhagavato citakaá¹ƒ Äá¸·impessÄmÄâ€™â€™ti na sakkonti Äá¸·impetuá¹ƒ. 233.At that time, four Malla chieftains, having bathed their heads and dressed in new clothes, thinking, "We will ignite the Blessed One's pyre," were unable to ignite it. Then the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ said to Venerable Anuruddha, "Venerable Anuruddha, what is the reason, what is the cause, that these four Malla chieftains, having bathed their heads and dressed in new clothes, thinking, 'We will ignite the Blessed One's pyre,' are unable to do so?" "VÄseá¹­á¹­has, the deities have a different intention." "But, Venerable, what is the intention of the deities?" "VÄseá¹­á¹­has, the deities' intention is this: 'This Venerable MahÄkassapa is traveling from PÄvÄ to KusinÄrÄ on the road, accompanied by a large Saá¹…gha of bhikkhus, about five hundred bhikkhus in all. The Blessed One's pyre shall not blaze until Venerable MahÄkassapa has bowed to the Blessed One's feet with his head.'" "Venerable, let it be as the deities intend."

234. Atha kho ÄyasmÄ mahÄkassapo yena kusinÄrÄ makuá¹­abandhanaá¹ƒ nÄma mallÄnaá¹ƒ cetiyaá¹ƒ, yena bhagavato citako tenupasaá¹…kami; upasaá¹…kamitvÄ ekaá¹ƒsaá¹ƒ cÄ«varaá¹ƒ katvÄ aÃ±jaliá¹ƒ paá¹‡ÄmetvÄ tikkhattuá¹ƒ citakaá¹ƒ padakkhiá¹‡aá¹ƒ katvÄ bhagavato pÄde sirasÄ vandi. TÄnipi kho paÃ±cabhikkhusatÄni ekaá¹ƒsaá¹ƒ cÄ«varaá¹ƒ katvÄ aÃ±jaliá¹ƒ paá¹‡ÄmetvÄ tikkhattuá¹ƒ citakaá¹ƒ padakkhiá¹‡aá¹ƒ katvÄ bhagavato pÄde sirasÄ vandiá¹ƒsu. Vandite ca panÄyasmatÄ mahÄkassapena tehi ca paÃ±cahi bhikkhusatehi sayameva bhagavato citako pajjali.

234.Then the Venerable MahÄkassapa went to the Mallas' shrine called Makuá¹­abandhana in KusinÄrÄ, where the Blessed One's pyre was. Having approached, he arranged his robe over one shoulder, raised his joined hands in salutation, circumambulated the pyre three times, and bowed his head at the Blessed One's feet. Those five hundred monks also arranged their robes over one shoulder, raised their joined hands in salutation, circumambulated the pyre three times, and bowed their heads at the Blessed One's feet. And when the Venerable MahÄkassapa and those five hundred monks had paid homage, the Blessed One's pyre ignited by itself.

235. JhÄyamÄnassa kho pana bhagavato sarÄ«rassa yaá¹ƒ ahosi chavÄ«ti vÄ cammanti vÄ maá¹ƒsanti vÄ nhÄrÅ«ti vÄ lasikÄti vÄ, tassa neva chÄrikÄ paÃ±Ã±Äyittha, na masi; sarÄ«rÄneva avasissiá¹ƒsu. TesaÃ±ca paÃ±cannaá¹ƒ dussayugasatÄnaá¹ƒ dveva dussÄni na á¸ayhiá¹ƒsu yaÃ±ca sabbaabbhantarimaá¹ƒ yaÃ±ca bÄhiraá¹ƒ. Daá¸á¸he ca kho pana bhagavato sarÄ«re antalikkhÄ udakadhÄrÄ pÄtubhavitvÄ bhagavato citakaá¹ƒ nibbÄpesi. UdakasÄlatopi [udakaá¹ƒ sÄlatopi (sÄ«. syÄ. kaá¹ƒ.)] abbhunnamitvÄ bhagavato citakaá¹ƒ nibbÄpesi. KosinÄrakÄpi mallÄ sabbagandhodakena bhagavato citakaá¹ƒ nibbÄpesuá¹ƒ. Atha kho kosinÄrakÄ mallÄ bhagavato sarÄ«rÄni sattÄhaá¹ƒ sandhÄgÄre sattipaÃ±jaraá¹ƒ karitvÄ dhanupÄkÄraá¹ƒ parikkhipÄpetvÄ [parikkhipitvÄ (syÄ.)] naccehi gÄ«tehi vÄditehi mÄlehi gandhehi sakkariá¹ƒsu garuá¹ƒ kariá¹ƒsu mÄnesuá¹ƒ pÅ«jesuá¹ƒ.

235.And as the Blessed One's body was burning, whatever was skin, or hide, or flesh, or sinew, or fluidâ€”no ashes or soot were seen; only the relics remained. Just as when ghee or oil is burning, no ashes or soot are seen, so too, as the Blessed One's body was burning, whatever was skin, or hide, or flesh, or sinew, or fluidâ€”no ashes or soot were seen; only the relics remained. And of those five hundred pairs of cloths, only two clothsâ€”the innermost and outermostâ€”were not consumed. Then, when the Blessed One's body had been burned, a stream of water from the sky appeared and extinguished the pyre. A water spout also rose up from the sal trees, extinguishing the pyre. The Mallas of KusinÄrÄ too extinguished the pyre with all kinds of fragrant water. Then the Mallas of KusinÄrÄ kept the Blessed One's relics in their council hall, surrounded them with a lattice of spears, and enclosed them with a rampart of bows. For seven days, they honored, revered, esteemed, and venerated them with dance, song, music, garlands, and perfumes.

Sabbeva bhonto sahitÄ samaggÄ,SammodamÄnÄ karomaá¹­á¹­habhÄge;VitthÄrikÄ hontu disÄsu thÅ«pÄ,BahÅ« janÄ cakkhumato pasannÄâ€™â€™ti.

â€œLet all of you, sirs, united and in harmony, rejoicing together, let us make eight shares; May stupas be widespread in all directions, so that many people may have faith in the One with Vision.â€

238. â€˜â€˜Tena hi, brÄhmaá¹‡a, tvaÃ±Ã±eva bhagavato sarÄ«rÄni aá¹­á¹­hadhÄ samaá¹ƒ savibhattaá¹ƒ vibhajÄhÄ«â€™â€™ti. â€˜â€˜Evaá¹ƒ, bhoâ€™â€™ti kho doá¹‡o brÄhmaá¹‡o tesaá¹ƒ saá¹…ghÄnaá¹ƒ gaá¹‡Änaá¹ƒ paá¹­issutvÄ bhagavato sarÄ«rÄni aá¹­á¹­hadhÄ samaá¹ƒ suvibhattaá¹ƒ vibhajitvÄ te saá¹…ghe gaá¹‡e etadavoca â€“ â€˜â€˜imaá¹ƒ me bhonto tumbaá¹ƒ dadantu ahampi tumbassa thÅ«paÃ±ca mahaÃ±ca karissÄmÄ«â€™â€™ti. ## DhÄtuthÅ«papÅ«jÄ

### Veneration of the Stupas of Relics.

239.Then King AjÄtasattu of Magadha, son of the VidehÄ«, built a stupa for the Blessed Oneâ€™s relics and held a great festival at RÄjagaha. 240. Aá¹­á¹­hadoá¹‡aá¹ƒ cakkhumato sarÄ«raá¹ƒ, sattadoá¹‡aá¹ƒ jambudÄ«pe mahenti.

240.The body of the One with Vision is eight measures; seven measures are venerated in JambudÄ«pa.

EkaÃ±ca doá¹‡aá¹ƒ purisavaruttamassa, rÄmagÄme nÄgarÄjÄ maheti.

And one measure of the foremost of men, the NÄga king venerates at RÄmagÄma.

EkÄhi dÄá¹­hÄ tidivehi pÅ«jitÄ, ekÄ pana gandhÄrapure mahÄ«yati;KÄliá¹…garaÃ±Ã±o vijite punekaá¹ƒ, ekaá¹ƒ pana nÄgarÄjÄ maheti.

One tooth is worshipped by the devas in TÄvatiá¹ƒsa, another is honored in the city of GandhÄra; yet another is in the realm of the Kalinga king, and one is venerated by the NÄga king.

Tasseva tejena ayaá¹ƒ vasundharÄ,Ä€yÄgaseá¹­á¹­hehi mahÄ« alaá¹…katÄ;Evaá¹ƒ imaá¹ƒ cakkhumato sarÄ«raá¹ƒ,Susakkataá¹ƒ sakkatasakkatehi.

By his very splendor, this earth is adorned, the ground embellished with the foremost objects of worship. Thus, this body of the One with Vision is well-honored, honored by those worthy of honor.

DevindanÄgindanarindapÅ«jito,Manussindaseá¹­á¹­hehi tatheva pÅ«jito;Taá¹ƒ vandatha [taá¹ƒ taá¹ƒ vandatha (syÄ.)] paÃ±jalikÄ labhitvÄ,Buddho have kappasatehi dullabhoti.

Worshipped by lords of devas, lords of nÄgas, and lords of men, likewise honored by the foremost of human lords. Having obtained (this opportunity), venerate him with joined palms, for indeed, a Buddha is hard to find even in hundreds of aeons.

CattÄlÄ«sa samÄ dantÄ, kesÄ lomÄ ca sabbaso;DevÄ hariá¹ƒsu ekekaá¹ƒ, cakkavÄá¸·aparamparÄti.

Forty teeth were equal, and all the hairs and body hairs; the devas took them away one by one, from universe to universe.

### The Great Discourse on the Final NibbÄna, the third section, is concluded.
